Jamison Brereton

2 (443)
Agni
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
11 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh, except ┼Ыakvar─л 11
In its first half (vss. 1тАУ5) this hymn echoes the themes of VI.1: Agni as the joint con cern of all the separate units of ─Аrya society (and indeed of the gods as well) and the success that attends the man who fulfills his ritual responsibilities to Agni. The hymn ends the same way (vss. 10тАУ11), with special mention of AgniтАЩs position in the individual house as well as his role as clanlord. The similarity between beginning and ending is marked by a signal of ring composition: the god Mitra compared to Agni in both the first and last verses. Agni is often compared with or identified with Mitra (тАЬAlly, AllianceтАЭ) because of his position on earth as guest and helper of men, though himself a god, and because, as god, he mediates the sacrificial alliance between gods and men.
By contrast, the verses in between (6тАУ9) offer a sequence of increasingly dense and complex images of fire, starting with a simple one of whirling smoke and sun like brightness (vs. 6), but the comparisons in verses 7cdтАУ8 rely on multiple puns and terse and elliptical phraseology. This middle section sets the stage for the rest of the Agni cycle with its focus on the physical aspects of fire.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou alight, Agni, like Mitra, upon the oblation offered with the dry fuel; therefore, beholder of all, possessor of riches, you cherish us with food and nourishment.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, o Agni, like Mitra are indeed master of the glory belonging to the settlements.
You prosper fame like prosperity, o good one without boundaries.

Jamison Brereton Notes

jy├│k cid atti g├бrbho y├бd ├бcyutam тАЬFor a long time the embryo eats just what is immovable.тАЭ Renou supplies a different verb in a from the one he supplies in b: тАЬ(tu ├йbranles) тАж comme le b├йtail (d├йvore) тАжтАЭ But this violates the structure of the RVic simile.

The problem in the 2nd hemistich is the form dh─Б╠Бm─Б. Grassmann, fld. by Lubotsky, interprets it as a 1st pl. root aor. injunctive, but though a 1st person would work in some hymns, there seems to be no personal intrusion in this one – nor can I figure out how a 1st pl. тАЬwe establish(ed)тАЭ would fit here. Both Geldner and Renou take it as a neut.

pl. to dh─Б╠Бman- and therefore the subject of vс╣Ы┼Ыc├бnti. However, this requires an interpr.

of dh─Б╠Бman- – Geldner тАЬKr├дfte,тАЭ Renou тАЬpouvoirs-dтАЩ├йtatтАЭ (whatever that means) – that I do not think is possible for this word, and, in any case, can тАЬpowersтАЭ hew? On the basis of VI.6.1 (also in this cycle) vс╣Ы┼Ыc├бdvana- тАШwood-hewingтАЩ (the compounded version of our v├бn─Б vс╣Ы┼Ыc├бnti), which modifies Agni, I think that the subject of vс╣Ы┼Ыc├бnti must be Agni, or rather some parts of Agni, since a plural is required. I therefore take ┼Ы├нkvasaс╕е as a nom. pl., not gen. sg. (with Geldner, Renou), referring to AgniтАЩs flames or his various embodiments. Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMen verily worship you with sacrifice and with praises; the inoffensive sun, the sender of rain, the beholder of the universe, proceeds to you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

It is said that the sun, at the evening enters into fire, therefore the latter is visible throughout the night; the term for sun in the text is, v─Бjin, he who goes swiftly; this is an appellative also of fire and wind: Agnirv─Бyuс╕е s┼лryas te vai v─Бjinaс╕е, fire, wind, the sun, they verily are v─Бjins (Taittir─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.6.3.9)

Jamison Brereton

It is you then that the boundaried domains reverently invoke, with sacrifices and with hymns;
to you drives the prizewinning (horse), avoiding the wolf, crossing (the mid)space, the one common to all the boundaried domains.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I doubt that the v─Бj├нn- of the 2nd hemistich is just any horse. It could be a mythical horse: Dadhikr─Б is called v─Бj├нn- vi┼Ыv├бkс╣Ыс╣гс╣нi- тАЬa prize-winner belonging to all communitiesтАЭ in IV.38.2. Or a god, perhaps Soma, Indra, or the Sun.

Griffith

For, verily, men pray to thee with sacrifices and with songs.
To thee the Friendly Courser, seen of all, comes speeding through the air.

Geldner

Denn dich rufen die Leute mit Opfergebeten und Lobreden an, zu dir kommt das Siegesro├Я, das dem Wolf entgeht und weite Strecken zur├╝cklegt, das in allen Landen bekannt ist.

Grassmann

Denn dich ja ehrt der Menschen Schar mit Liedern und mit Opfern hoch; Zu dir geht hin das Segensross, die, Luft durchdringend, allen hold.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe offerers of praise, sympathizing in satisfaction, kindle you the banner of the sacrifice, when man, the descendant of Manu, desiring happiness, invokes you to the rite.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In concert the men of heaven kindle you as beacon of the sacrifice, when the human race here, seeking favor, has called upon (you) in the ceremony.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take juhv├й to тИЪhu тАШpour, offerтАЩ, but this causes a problem with the main cl. verb, the pres. indhate тАШkindleтАЩ, if we assume that the pf. of тИЪhu has some kind of preterital sense. It does not make ritual sense to offer the melted butter in the fire before kindling it. Geldner avoids the problem by translating with a present, but this is ad hoc. With S─Бyaс╣Зa. I take the verb to тИЪhv─Б тАШcallтАЩ instead, since invocations can be and regularly are made after the fire is kindled. Although K├╝mmel follows the тИЪhu interpr. (605), he admits that the alternative should be seriously considered (n. 1316).

It might be objected that a pf. to the seс╣н root тИЪhv─Б should be read trisyllabically (juhu ve), as it indeed is in X.149.5, but as K├╝mmel points out (n. 1317), an undoubted 3rd sg. pf. to тИЪhv─Б, juhve in I.32.6, is disyllabic. (The sequencing of actions problem with тИЪidh – тИЪhu could be avoided if the former means something like тАШfan the flamesтАЩ, an action that could indeed follow the pouring of the butter into a banked fire. But I donтАЩt know that we have any evidence for this sense – beyond the fact that indhate belongs to a pres. stem and could have durative value.) For further support for my interpr. of this vs. see immed. below.

Griffith

Of one accord men kindle thee Heaven’s signal of the sacrifice,
When, craving bliss, this race of man invites thee to the solemn rite.

Geldner

Dich, das Wahrzeichen des Opfers, entflammen eintr├дglich die Mannen des Himmels, wenn dieses Menschenkind deine Gunst begehrend im Gottesdienst opfert.

Grassmann

Des Himmels M├дnner z├╝nden dich, des Opfers Licht, vereinigt an, Sobald das menschliche Geschlecht beim Feste opfert liebevoll.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the mortal prosper who propitiates you (his) benefactor, by holy rites; through the protection of you who are resplendent, he overcomes those who hate him, as if they were mortal sins.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The mortal who will bring (the sacrifice) to fulfillment with his insight and will perform ritual labor for you of good gifts,
with the help of lofty heaven he crosses hatreds like narrow straits.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The problematic form in this vs. is the first word с╣Ы╠Бdhat. It clearly belongs with the root aor. attested primarily in the opt. (с╣Ыdhy─Б╠Бma, etc.) but also found once in the participle с╣Ыdh├бnt-, with expected suffixal accent. It is the root accent that distinguishes the form here. Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.279 = KlSch 738; also Noten) suggests that it is a neut. part. used adverbially, with accent shift (*с╣Ыdh├бt ├а с╣Ы╠Бdhat) – claiming that adverbial accent shift can go either way, simply marking an oppositional formation. But the standard exx. (drav├бt to dr├бvati) involve a rightward shift, and in any case the whole notion of adverbial accent shift has recently been called into question (see Emily BarthтАЩs Cornell diss.). Renou considers both possibilities and opts finally for the adverb, while Geldner takes it as a finite form. I prefer to take it as an aor.

subjunctive (see also Lubotsky, Concordance, where it is so identified) parallel to ┼Ыa┼Ы├бmate. Although I cannot entirely explain the zero-grade root syllable for expected full-grade *├бrdhat (though see below), I can suggest a local explanation for the (supposedly) unexpected root accent. The next hymn contains the hapax verbalgoverning cmpd. с╣Ыdh├бd-v─Бra- тАШbringing wishes to successтАЩ. Whatever the original grammatical identity of the 1st members of this fairly common cmpd. type, synchronically they appear to be neut. sg. participles in -├бt with accent consistently on the suffix (type bhar├бd-v─Бja- [in fact, the name of the poet of this hymn and of the VIth Maс╣Зс╕Нala in general], dh─Бray├бt-kavi-, etc.; see AiG II.1.317-20), and the verbal stems from which they are derived regularly are accented one syllable to the left. So, for the examples just given, 1st class pres. bh├бrati, -├бya-formation dh─Бr├бyati, etc. I would therefore suggest that our poet, who had с╣Ыdh├бt-v─Бra- in his repertoire, backformed the root-accented finite form с╣Ы╠Бdhat on this model. A possibly simpler alternative is to begin with a hypothetical root aorist paradigm, whose injunctive act.

sg. *├бrdham, *├бrd/t, *├бrd/t should have full grade and root accent and whose subjunctive should likewise have both: *├бrdh─Б(ni), *├бrdhas(i), *├бrdhat(i) (cf. injunc.

k├бr and subj. k├бrati, e.g.). As it happens, the root aor. of тИЪс╣Ыdh is attested only in forms where we expect zero-grade root and suffixal accent, but the starred forms just given are the paradigmatically expected act. sg. forms. Under this explanation, the root accent of subjunctive *с╣Ы╠Бdhat is not the problem; its zero grade is. And we can explain that either by the influence (at time of composition or of redaction) of с╣Ыdh├бdv─Бra- in VI.3.2 or by the absence of other attested full-grade verbal forms to this root (though cf. gerundive ├бrdhya-) and consequent generalization of the zero-grade. Of the two explanations just given, I mildly favor the first - in part because the poet Bharadv─Бja would have been acutely aware of the accentual properties of his name.

A minor support for the interpr. of с╣Ы╠Бdhat as finite subjunctive, not adverbially used participle is provided by formulaics. As Renou sketches, тИЪс╣Ыdh can take yaj├▒├бm as object; cf. X.110.2 m├бnm─Бni dh─лbh├нr ut├б yaj├▒├бm r╠еndh├бn тАЬbringing the thoughts and the sacrifice to fulfillment through his visionary thoughts.тАЭ The VP yaj├▒├бm тИЪс╣Ыdh тАЬbring sacrifice to fulfillmentтАЭ can be seen as a variant of simplex тИЪyaj тАШsacrificeтАЩ, and тИЪyaj and тИЪ┼Ыam form a conjoined pair for our poet in nearby hymns: VI.1.9 s├│ agne ─лje ┼Ыa┼Ыame ca m├бrto тАЬO Agni, that mortal has sacrificed and ritually laboredтАЭ and VI.3.2 (the same vs. that contains с╣Ыdh├бdv─Бra-) ─лj├й yaj├▒├йbhiс╕е ┼Ыa┼Ыam├й ┼Ы├бm─лbhiс╕е тАЬhe has sacrificed with sacrifices, he has labored with ritual labors.тАЭ X.110.2 quoted above also suggests that, despite the p─Бda break, dhiy─Б╠Бin our passage is better construed with с╣Ы╠Бdhat as in the published translation than with ┼Ыa┼Ыamate with, e.g., Geldner тАЬтАж (und) mit Andacht den Dienst versieht.тАЭ Note the sandhi ┼лt─л╠Бс╣г├б, with retroflexion despite the lack of a close syntactic connection, as well as the unusual position of ordinarily p─Бda-init. s├б. An incomplete collection of relevant passages shows that this retroflexion of non-initial s├б in ruki contexts is standard but not invariable: IV.26.4 pr├б s├║ с╣г├б …, VI.2.4 ┼лt─л╠Бс╣г├б …, VI.14.1 bh├бsan n├║ с╣г├б …, VI.20.5 ur├║ с╣г├б тАж, VII.104.10 n├н с╣г├б …, VIII.20.16 abh├н с╣г├б …, IX.73.8 tr─л╠Бс╣г├б …, IX.79.3 … ar├нr h├н с╣г├б. But I.64.13 pr├б n┼л╠Бs├б …, without ruki.

English translation:

тАЬThe mortal who feeds your consecrated burnt offering with fuel enjoys, Agni, a dwelling peopled with descendants, and a life of a hundred years.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The mortal who after kindling (you) will achieve the offering to you and the whetting of you,
he prospers his dwelling place, (so that it has many) branches and
hundred(-year) lifespans, o Agni.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two adjectives vay─Б╠Бvantam and ┼Ыat─Б╠Бyuс╣гam are best taken as proleptic, with Geldner and Renou

For extensive disc. of this vss., see comm. ad VI.2.4-5 above.

The mortal who with fuel lights thy flame and offers unto thee,

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдГ рджреАрдкреНрддрд╕реНрдп рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд╢реБрдХреНрд░рдГ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд▓рдГ рд╢реБрднреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрдгреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдзреВрдордГ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдЖрддрддрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдЛрдгреНрд╡рддрд┐ рдореЗрдШрд╛рддреНрдордирд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рдгрддреЛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╣реЗ рдкрд╛рд╡рдХ рд╢реЛрдзрдХрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕реВрд░реЛ рди рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрд╡ рдХреГрдкрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреАрдХрд░рдгрд╕рдорд░реНрдердпрд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рджреНрдпреБрддрд╛ рджреАрдкреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рд░реЛрдЪрд╕реЗ рд╣рд┐ рджреАрдкреНрдпрд╕реЗ рдЦрд▓реБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe pure smoke of you the resplendent spreads through the firmament, matures (in clouds), and you, the purifier, shine with radiance like the sun, when propitiated by praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Shine with radiance: dyut─Б tvam kс╣Ыp─Б rocase, you shine with light by praise; kс╣Ыp─Б may also denote d─лpty─Б, with lustre; here, it is explained as stuty─Б, by praise, by that which is able to compel the presence of a deity, abhimukh─лkaraс╣Зa s─Бmarthya (Nirukta 6,8); kс╣Ыp also means to be able or capable, s─Бmarthyena, dipty─Б v─Б, by ability, power, or by lustre

Jamison Brereton

Your smoke, when it is in heaven, is turbulent in motion, stretched out (there) gleaming,
for you shine with your body, o pure one, like the sun with its brilliance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Just as in VI.1.2 there is a nom. sg. masc. pres. part. s├бn without any obvious concessive value; unlike VI.1.2 there is no metrical explanation available. The close sandhi in the phrase div├н с╣г├бn might seem to give us a clue – that the two words should be read as a constituent and are the equivalent of a circumstantial clause: constituency could account for the ruki. This is responsible for my tr. тАЬwhen it is in heavenтАЭ (sim. Geldner), instead of construing div├н with ─Б╠Бtataс╕е like Renou (тАЬsтАЩ├йtendant au cielтАЭ). However, assembling the retroflexion data both for s├бn/s├бt in a ruki environment and for div├н with following s- weakens this hypothesis. In the former case s├бn/s├бd generally doesnтАЩt exhibit retroflexion; see III.9.2 d┼лr├й s├бn, IV.15.1 v─Бj─л╠Б s├бn, IV.27.1 n├║ s├бn, VIII.43.9 g├бrbhe s├бn (though the first and third phrases are constituents); V.44.3 sacate s├бd, VI.27.2 m├бde s├бd + niс╣г├бdi s├бt + vividre s├бd, X.129.1 n├│ s├бd. However, there is retroflexion in II.41.10 abh─л╠Бс╣г├бd; ├бnti с╣г├бd IV.5.10, VIII.73.1 (though the two forms don’t form a syntactic constituent in any of these passages) and in IX.61.10 div├н с╣г├бd (almost exactly our phrase). In other words, the data are equivocal. On the other hand, the loc. div├н regularly retroflexes the initial sof forms of тИЪas, as here: I.108.11 div├н с╣гс╣нh├│ [dual verb], V.2.10 div├н с╣гantu, V.60.6 div├н с╣гс╣нh├б, VI.33.5 div├н с╣гy─Бma, and the just cited IX.61.10 (cf. also VI.52.13 dy├бvi с╣гс╣нha), though it does not retroflex other initial s-s; cf. I.125.6 div├н s┼л╠Бryasya, V.27.6 = V.85.2 div├н s┼л╠Бryam, V.35.8 div├н st├│mam, VIII.56.5 div├н s┼л╠Бryo, X.75.3 div├н svan├│, X.85.1 div├н s├│mo. It thus appears that the retroflexion of с╣г├бn here is an automatic product of a rule that induces ruki in s-initial forms of the verb тАШto beтАЩ after div├н and does not give information – or at least high-quality information – about constituency.

I have no idea why тИЪas should exhibit this behavior; it cannot be due to (lack of) accent, since several of the ruki-ed forms are accented (including the one here).

Michael Weiss comments: тАЬBut maybe it was despite its accent somehow a clitic just as there are accented 2nd pos. clit. This reminds me of the loss of s in Oldenberg Latin comedy which is especially well attested before the verb тАШto beтАЩ.тАЭ

Griffith

Thy bright smoke lifts itself aloft, and far-extended shines in heaven.
For, Purifier! like the Sun thou beamest with thy radiant glow.

Geldner

Heftig steigt dein Rauch auf, hell sich ausbreitend, wenn er am Himmel ist, denn wie die Sonne in ihrem Glanz, so leuchtest du in deiner Sch├╢nheit, du Lauterer.

Grassmann

Es wirbelt auf dein heller Rauch am Himmel leuchtend, ausgedehnt; Denn du erstrahlst, o Flammender, an Glanz und Ansehn sonnengleich.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou are now to be praised among the people, for you are our well beloved guest, venerated like an elder in the city, and to be cherished like a son.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Venerated like an elder in a city: raс╣Зvaс╕е pur─лva j┼лryaс╕е s┼лnur na trayay─Бyyaс╕е; the first part is interpreted nagary─Бm vс╣Ыddho hitopadeс╣гс╣н─Б r─Бj─Б iva ramaс╣З─лyaс╕е, to be had recourse to as to an old r─Бj─Б giving good council in a city; the second half, putra iva p─Бlan─лyaс╕е, to be cherished like a son; or, trayay─Бyya may be explained as endowed with three merits, learning, penance, devotion; or one having had three births, the natural, investiture with the sacred string, and initiation or preparation for sacred rites, d─лkс╣г─Б: m─Бturagredhijananam dvit─лyam bhaunjibandhan─Бt tс╣Ыt─лyam yaj├▒a d─лkс╣г─Бy─Б iti janmatrayam smс╣Ыtam (Manu. 2.169)

Jamison Brereton

For now you are to be reverently invoked among the clans, as our dear guest,
to be protected like a son who brings delight to the home, (but also) to be enflamed like a battle-lusty (warrior) in a stronghold.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd hemistich presents some interpretational problems, generated by the standard assumption that j┼л╠Бrya- belongs to тИЪjс╣Ы тАШbe/get oldтАЩ. Not only is the expression тАЬdelightful like an aged one in his strongholdтАЭ odd, but such interpr.

require bleaching out the gerundive value of j┼л╠Бrya- (esp. unlikely given that itтАЩs parallel to trayay─Б╠Бyyaс╕е in d and ─л╠Бс╕Нyaс╕е in a). Cf., e.g., GeldnerтАЩs тАЬbehaglich [cozy, snug] wie ein Greis in seiner Burg,тАЭ which also pushes raс╣Зv├б- into a meaning otherwise unknown to it. RenouтАЩs тАЬjoyeux, tel un vieil (homme) dans la forteresseтАЭ maintains the meaning of raс╣Зv├б-, but the connection between it and the simile seems strained. Oldenberg (ZDMG 55: 279 = KlSch 738) cleverly suggests that thereтАЩs a crisscross word order, with the son of the simile in d appropriate to the adj. in c and vice versa: so something like (he doesnтАЩt actually translate) тАЬdelightful like a son, to be protected like an old man in his stronghold.тАЭ But this is an ad hoc response to dissatisfaction with the apparent pragmatics of the passage.

These problems can be solved in twofold fashion. 1) I take raс╣Зv├бс╕е as a pun, a word common to both similes. In both cases it applies to Agni, but in two different senses. 2) This reinterpretation is enabled by a different analysis of j┼л╠Бrya-. I take it to the root тИЪjvar тАШburn, flameтАЩ, showing the same zero-grade as in j┼лrс╣З├н- тАШfirebrandтАЩ (тЖР*jvс╣ЫH-C, with loss of -v- before ┼л/u, as in ur├║- тЖР *vс╣ЫH-u). I can see no possible formal objection to this analysis, despite the apparently universal insistence that j┼л╠Бrya- must belong to тИЪjс╣Ы.

Starting with these assumptions, we can take the two gerundives, j┼л╠Бryaс╕е in c and trayay─Б╠Бyyah in d, as the predicates of their respective p─Бdas (as ─л╠Бс╕Нyaс╕е is of p─Бda a). One of the drawbacks to the standard interpr. is that this syntactic parallelism is broken. In c the picture is of an battle-eager (warrior) (for a similar usage of raс╣Зv├бsee X.115.4 and remember that r├бс╣Зa- means both тАШjoyтАЩ and тАШbattleтАЩ) who is to be enflamed / set blazing; in the simile j┼л╠Бrya- is metaphorical, but of course the word is literally applicable to Agni the fire, who is the upameya, the target of the simile. One minor problem with this interpr. is that the simile marker iva is in the wrong position: we would expect to find it after raс╣Зv├б-. But there are enough displaced simile markers in the RV that this positioning is not a major obstacle.

When applied to the simile in d, raс╣Зv├б- has its more usual meaning тАШdelightful, bringing delightтАЩ, which is appropriate to the son and helps explain the desire to protect him. Here the published translation adds тАЬto the homeтАЭ to тАЬa son who brings delight.тАЭ I made this addition because I think thereтАЩs a buried pun. On the one hand, in c raс╣Зv├бс╕е pur├н (тАЬbattle-lusty warrior in a fortressтАЭ) construes a locative with the subject (acdg. to my view of the constituency) and we might expect a similar loc. in the corresponding expression; on the other, raс╣Зv├б- in its meaning тАШdelightfulтАЩ is often a descriptor of a home or construed with a loc. of тАШhomeтАЩ. Cf. I.69.4-5 raс╣Зv├│ duroс╣З├й тАЬbringing joy to the house,тАЭ precisely of Agni. It may be that p┼лr├н can be directly applied to the simile in d and in that context means тАШhomeтАЩ – though I doubt it: RVic p├║r- does not have domestic associations. Instead I think that raс╣Зv├б- in the тАЬprotected sonтАЭ context evokes duroс╣З├й, and this subsurface evocation is realized in the next verse by the phonologically similar loc. dr├│с╣Зe тАШwood(en) cupтАЩ. The unexpected and unusual use of dr├│с╣Зa- in that vs. (for which see comm. ad loc.) suggests that it may have been deployed there in order to play on the unexpressed (*)duroс╣З├й here. This may seem overclever; in that case the tr. could stop short at тАЬto be protected like a son who brings delight.тАЭ In any case, it would probably better to put тАЬto the homeтАЭ in parens.

A last comment on the hemistich: I have tr. cd in the opposite order, so that the domestic half (d) immediately adjoins the тАЬdear guestтАЭ of b. This is not necessary, but given that my interpr. of c involves a radical rethinking of the standard view, it seemed best to make the new reading easier to assimilate.

The gerundive of d, trayay─Б╠Бyi ya-, is a hapax and a striking formation – in the first instance, just because of the rhythmic rollout of -VyV- sequences. With regard to its derivation, as Debrunner points out (AiG II.2.285-86), it seems to pattern with

-─Б╠Бyya- gerundives built to -├бya-stems: panay─Б╠Бyya-, mahay─Б╠Бyya-, spс╣Ыhay─Б╠Бyya-.

However, there is no such verb stem *tray├бya-. Debrunner adds the parenthetical remark тАЬvon v. Pr├дs. tr─Бya-,тАЭ but of course in that case we should expect *tr─Бy─Б╠Бyya-.

Both the short root vowel and the extra -ya- remain unexplained by that derivation. I have only the wispiest gestures towards an explanation. For тИЪtr─Б we would probably expect an -├бya-formation *tr─Бpaya-; however, it might have followed the model of тИЪp─Б and тИЪpy─Б with a -y-hiatus filler instead (p─Бy├бyati and py─Бy├бyati [AV+] respectively), hence *tr─Бy├бyati. We might then invoke the tendency of roots with the shape CR─Б to shorten their root vowel in the p-causative, type j├▒apayati and, specifically with Cr─Б root, ┼Ыrap├бyati (both AV+). For disc. see my 1983 monograph on the -├бya-formations, pp. 208-11. So one might posit such a shortening to the differently formed causative to a CR─Б root *tray├бyati, which could serve as base for our trayay─Б╠Бyya- here (encouraged by the short root vowels of the -├бya-stem -─Б╠Бyyagerundives quoted above). But the chain of assumptions and unattested forms seems too long, and we might instead just attribute trayay─Б╠Бyi ya- to a poetтАЩs whimsical multiplication of -ya-s – his version of tra-la-la. Michael Weiss suggests: тАЬFrom i-extended form of *terh1- ‘rub’ (Lat. trivi, etc.), with double sense тАШto be rubbedтАЩ, i.e., caressed, and also referring to the fire drill?тАЭ This is an appealing suggestion, but the lack of other representatives of this root in IIr. might disfavor it.

Griffith

For in men’s houses thou must be glorified as a well-loved guest,
Gay like an elder in a fort, claiming protection like a son.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдХреНрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рдордиреНрдердирд░реВрдкреЗрдг рджреНрд░реЛрдгреЗ рджреНрд░реБрдореЗ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдареЗрд╜рд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдЬреНрдпрд╕реЗ рд╣рд┐ рд╡реНрдпрдЬреНрдпрд╕реЗ рдЦрд▓реБ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рди рд╡реЗрдЬрдирд╡рд╛рдирд╢реНрд╡ рдЗрд╡ рдХреГрддреНрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред рдХреГрддреНрд╡реАрддрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдордирд╛рдо ред рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╣рдирд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╛ ред рд╕ рдпрдерд╛ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдВ рд╡рд╣рддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рджреНрдзрд╡рд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╣рдирдордЧреНрдиреЗрд░рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рд╛рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рдЬреНрдореЗрд╡ рдкрд░рд┐рддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд░рд┐рд╡ рджрд╛рд╡рд╛рдирд▓рд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкреЗрдг рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд╛ ред рдЕрдиреНрдирдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рдЕрдиреНрдирдВ рдЧрдпрдГ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдЪ рднрд╡рд╕рд┐ ред рдЙрднрдпреЛрд░реНрджрд╛рддреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╢рд┐рд╢реБрдГ рдЬрд╛рддрдорд╛рддреНрд░реЛ рдмрд╛рд▓реЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрддреНрдпреЛ рди рд╕рддрддрдЧрд╛рдореА рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрд╢реНрд╡ рдЗрд╡ рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдпрдГ рдХреБрдЯрд┐рд▓рдорд┐рддрд╕реНрддрддреЛ рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛рд╕рд┐ ред тАШрд╣реНрд╡реГ рдХреМрдЯрд┐рд▓реНрдпреЗ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдпреИрддрджреНрд░реВрдкрдореН рееред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou are manifested in the timber, Agni, by the act of attrition; you are the bearer (of the oblation) as a horse (is of his rider); you are like the circumsambient wind; you are food and dwelling; you are like a (newborn) babe, and variable (in movement) as a horse.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You are food and dwelling: svadh─Б gayaс╕е = annam gс╣Ыham ca; bhavasi, you are is supplied

Jamison Brereton

For according to your purpose you are anointed in the wood(en cup) (like soma) [/in your home =hearth] [/driven into the wood(en cup)] like a prize-seeker who gets results.
(You are) encompassing like a household (that encompasses all its
members) through your independent power; (you are) made to go in circles like a young steed (being trained).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. ├бgne was omitted in the published translation I would insert тАЬo AgniтАЭ after тАЬpurpose.тАЭ Note that the first hemistich begins with kr├бtv─Б and ends with kс╣Ы╠Бtvi yaс╕е.

This vs. displays the same verbal intricacy as the immediately preceding vs. 7.

As also in vs. 7 the first hemistich is less complex than the second, but that doesnтАЩt mean it lacks puzzles. The principal question is the root affiliation of ajy├бse. With Geldner, I take it as a pun, as passive to both тИЪa├▒j тАШanointтАЩ and тИЪaj тАШdriveтАЩ (Oldenberg opts for тИЪaj, Renou for тИЪa├▒j)тАФa pun that we also find frequently in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX. The primary connection is presumably to тИЪa├▒j: the ritual fire is тАЬanointedтАЭ with the offering butter; cf. the nearby occurrences of the ppl. akt├б- тАШanointedтАЩ (VI.4.6, 5.6). But the loc. dr├│с╣Зe casts a shadow on the clarity of this association. Though the stem dr├│с╣Зais doubtless a deriv. of d─Б╠Бru-/dr├║- тАШwoodтАЩ (see EWA s.v.), it doesnтАЩt refer to wood as a general material, much less to firewood. It is specialized as the (wooden) cup for soma; the stem is mostly limited to the Soma Maс╣Зс╕Нala, but even in its two other occurrences in VI (37.2, 44.20) it refers to the soma cup. Therefore, if we want to take dr├│с╣Зe ajy├бse here to mean something like тАЬ(the fire located) on the (fire-)wood is anointed,тАЭ we must take dr├│с╣Зe as a specialized stand-in for v├бne or the like (see the passages assembled by Geldner in n. 8a; cf. also druс╣г├бdv─Б тАШsitting on the woodтАЩ in the next hymn, VI.3.5), whose meaning has been twisted. This unusual substitution pushes us in two directions. On the one hand, if dr├│с╣Зe here is meant to evoke duroс╣З├й тАШat homeтАЩ in the previous vs. (7cd), we can explain its unusual employment here and the twisting of its referent from wooden cup to wood – and even take it as gesturing to тАШhomeтАЩ here as well, тАШhomeтАЩ being AgniтАЩs fireplace as well as the home of the sacrificer. On the other hand, since the soma after its purification is regularly driven into its containers, we can take ajy├бse also to тИЪaj тАШdriveтАЩ and see the common identification of the two ritual substances, fire and soma, that pervades much of the RV. One of the characteristic ritual actions performed on Soma would here be attributed to Agni. The simile in b, v─Бj─л╠Бn├б тАШlike a prize-seekerтАЩ works with either verb, since horses are both anointed and driven. Moreover, both v─Бj├нn- and kс╣Ы╠Бtvyaare regularly used of soma – further strengthening the Agni/Soma connection sketched in p─Бda a.

The similes in the next two p─Бdas cause further problems. In c the first question is the case of svadh─Б╠Б. Geldner and Oldenberg favor nom., Renou and I instr. If svadh─Б╠Бis nom., the series of similes with Agni as implicit subject and upameya is disrupted.

The next issue is what is meant by a p├бrijm─Б тАж g├бyaс╕е. Both Geldner and Renou take it as some sort of mobile home (e.g., Geldner тАЬein fahrender HausstandтАЭ). Although in a pastoral society like that of the RV such a notion is not as comic as it might at first seem тАФ and although fire is frequently depicted as burning across the land тАФ I do not think that that is the image meant there. Note first that g├бya- is several times associated with the preverb p├бri (esp. p├бri тИЪp─Б VI.71.3, X.66.3, though as an object not a subject, I have to admit). And from its literal sense тАШearth-encirclingтАЩ, p├бrijman- can develop the sense тАШencircling, encompassingтАЩ. That is the sense I see here, with the domestic deity Agni compared to the extended family that embraces everything belonging to it – a likely reference to the ritual fire as the joint possession and symbol of the ─Аrya clans.

The second simile depends on the meaning of hv─Бry├б-. This stem must belong to the root тИЪhvс╣Ы тАШgo crookedlyтАЩ. Geldner thinks it refers to a bird, which has little to recommend it since thereтАЩs already a horse in the passage; others (Renou, Thieme [KlSch 78]) to the meandering or zig-zag movement of the fire (e.g., Renou тАЬ(il va) zigzaguant тАжтАЭ). I prefer to take it as a gerundive (despite the accent, which is unusual for such a formation) and indeed one to an underlying causative. My further assumption is that the тАЬyoung steedтАЭ of the simile is being trained, by being run in circles (around someone in the middle holding a rope attached to the horse – a standard part of horse training today it seems from images and videos conjured up by Google – and recall the Mitanni horse-training tablets with their numbers of тАШturnsтАЩ [vartana]). Although тИЪhvс╣Ы often refers to more random motion, it implicitly contrasts with motion in a straight line, which a circle is not. The advantages to this interpr. are 1) it would refer to something that the ritual fire actually does or is made to do: the Paryagnikaraс╣Зa or the circling of the sacrificial animal (and associated paraphernalia) with a firebrand; 2) it would implicitly pick up p├бrijm─Б from the beginning of the hemistich, with a more literal sense of тАШencircle, encompassтАЩ than in p─Бda c. If this latter suggestion is correct, as in 7cd the first word of p─Бda c, p├бrijm─Б, would be applicable to the similes in both c and d with slightly different senses, just like raс╣Зv├бс╕е in 7c.

Griffith

Thou, Agni, like an able steed, art urged by wisdom in the wood.
Thou art like wind; food, home art thou, like a young horse that runs astray.

Geldner

Mit Umsicht wirst du ja im Holzgef├д├Я gesalbt zum Laufe getrieben wie ein siegesgewisses Rennpferd, o Agni. Wie ein fahrender Hausstand ist sein Wesen, wie ein Rennpferd ist der junge Vogel.

Grassmann

Zum Holze l├дsst du treiben dich, o Agni, wie ein schnelles Ross, W├дhlst selbst dein Haus dem Winde gleich, dem Renner gleich, der Schlange Kind.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou consume Agni, the unfallen (trees) as an animal (feeds) upon pasture, when, undecaying deity, the flames of you who are resplendent shear the forests.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You (eat) just these unstirrable things, Agni, like livestock in a pasture. (This is your) principle: that your dexterous (flames?) hew the woods, o unaging one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner, I supply the verb тАШeatтАЩ in p─Бda a. Although Geldner does not give his reasons, the existence of a parallel passage in this Agni cycle gives a clear warrant:

Griffith

E’en things imperishable, thou, O Agni, like a gazing ox,
Eatest, when hosts, Eternal One! of thee the Mighty rend the woods.

Geldner

Du fri├Яt selbst die festen H├╢lzer, o Agni, wie ein Tier das Gras auf der Weide, wenn deine, des Ge├╝bten, Kr├дfte die B├дume f├дllen, du Alterloser.

Grassmann

Das Feste auch bemeisterst du, verzehrend Agni, wie das Vieh, Wenn, Ew’ger, deine Flammenschar das Holz zerspaltet, starker du.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou enter as the ministrant priest into the habitations of men who wish to perform sacrifice; render them prosperous, benefactor of mankind; be propitiated, aс╣Еgiras, by the oblation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because you pursue (your ritual duties) as Hotar in the house for the clans who perform the ceremonies, o Agni,
make them unified, o clanlord; enjoy (our) oblation, o Aс╣Еgiras.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I interpr p─Бda a (which is identical to IV.9.5a) as a variation on passages like X.2.2 v├йс╣гi hotr├бm ut├б potr├бс╣Г j├бn─Бn─Бm тАЬpursue the office of Hotar and of Potar of the peoples,тАЭ but with gapping of the terms for the priestly offices.

The standard tr. take samс╣Ыdh├бс╕е as an abstract тАШsuccessтАЩ (e.g., Geldner тАЬSchaff тАж GelingenтАЭ; cf. also Renou, Scarlatta [67]), but the only other occurrences of this root noun, in the frog hymn VII.103.5, clearly means something like тАШunisonтАЩ, referring to the frog chorus. One of the two finite forms of this lexeme, s├бm ─Бnс╣Ыdhe in X.79.7, also seems to have this sense: Agni тАЬcomes togetherтАЭ with his parts or limbs (p├бrvabhiс╕е). The other, in X.85.27, has a sense closer to simplex тИЪс╣Ыdh тАШbe (completely) realized, come to successтАЩ. In our passage here, the тАШunisonтАЩ interpr. makes sense, esp. in the larger context of this hymns (and also VI.1), with the focus on Agni as clanlord of the separate ─Аrya clans, which are nonetheless working towards a common goal. On the other hand, the appearance of simplex с╣Ы╠Бdhat in this hymn (4a, on which see comm. ad loc.) and in the cmpd. с╣Ыdh├бdv─Бra- in the next (VI.3.2) might suggest a rendering closer to the simplex here as well.

Griffith

Agni, thou enterest as Priest the home of men who sacrifice.
Lord of the people, prosper them. Accept the ofrering, Angiras!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine Agni, reverenced as a friend, who are abiding in heaven and earth, communicate our praise to the gods; conduct the offerer of adoration to domestic felicity; and may we overcome our adversaries, our iniquities, our difficulties; may we overcome those (sins of a prior existence); may we overcome them by your protection.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May we overcome those (sins): the text has t─Б tarema, may we cross over those, this is interpreted as: janm─Бntarakс╣Ыt─Бni p─Бp─Бni

Jamison Brereton

O god Agni with the might of Mitra, to us you call the gods, call the grace of the two world-halves.
Pursue well-being, good dwelling, pursue the men of heaven. May we cross over hatreds, over narrow straits difficult to traverse.
May we cross over; with your help may we cross over.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this vs. forms a slight ring with vs. 1, with voc. mitramahaс╕е echoing mitr├│ n├б of 1b.

Both Geldner and Renou take v─лh├н as having a double acc., with svast├нс╣Г sukс╣гit├нm the secondary object expressing benefits we seek from the gods whom we pursue (e.g., Geldner тАЬErsuche die M├дnner des Himmels um Gl├╝ck, um gutes Wohnen.тАЭ But this seems unnecessary (and is not the usual syntax of тИЪv─л); the root тИЪv─л takes a variety of objects, including concrete inanimates, as in VI.12.6 (in this cycle) v├йс╣гi r─Бy├бс╕е тАЬyou pursue riches,тАЭ and here I see it as having both inanimate and animate objects.

P─Бda d dviс╣г├│ ├бс╣Гh─Бс╣Гsi durit─Б╠Бtarema is a reprise of 4d dviс╣г├│ ├бс╣Гho n├б tarati.

Griffith

O Agni, God with Mitra’s might, call hither the favour of the Gods from earth and heaven.
Bring weal from heaven, that men may dwell securely. May we o’ercome the foe’s malign oppressions, may we o’ercome them, through thy help o’ercome them.

Geldner

Lade, du wie Mitra gefeierter Gott, die G├╢tter zu uns ein, o Agni, erbitte die Gunst beider Welten! Ersuche die M├дnner des Himmels um Gl├╝ck, um gutes Wohnen! Wir m├╢chten ├╝ber die Anfeindungen, die N├╢te, die F├дhrlichkeiten hinwegkommen, wir m├╢chten ├╝ber diese hinwegkommen, durch deine Gnade hinwegkommen.

Grassmann

Rufe uns, o freundereicher Gott die G├╢tter her, o Agni, und das Wohlwollen beider Welten; f├╝hre die M├дnner des Himmels her zu Heil und Sicherheit; ├╝ber des Feindes Drangsale und Gefahren m├╢gen wir hin├╝berdringen, ├╝ber sie hin├╝berdringen, durch deine H├╝lfe hin├╝berdringen.

Elizarenkova

  • рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬреЛ рдмрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреНрдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдм рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдорд╣рдГ) рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдЖрджрд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдРрд╕реЗ (рджреЗрд╡) рджрд╛рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рдЬрди ! рдЖрдк (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рджрд╛рддрд╛ рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд░реЛрджрд╕реНрдпреЛрдГ) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рдФрд░ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдХреЗ рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ (рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдореН) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд╛ (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ (рд╡реЛрдЪрдГ) рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдХрд╛рд░рдг рд╕реЗ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦ рд╡рд╛ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ (рд╕реБрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд┐рдореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рд╡рд╛ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕ рдХреЛ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрд╛рдордирд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдФрд░ (рдиреДрдиреН) рдирд╛рдпрдХ рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╡реАрд╣рд┐) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реВрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ рдФрд░ (рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ) рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░реЛ рддрдерд╛ (рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛) рджреБрдГрдЦ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдЕрдВрд╣рд╛рд╕рд┐) рдкрд╛рдкреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рддрд░реЗрдо) рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ (рддрд╛) рдЙрдирдХреЛ (рддрд░реЗрдо) рдлрд┐рд░ рднреА рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрдВ рдФрд░ (рддрд╡) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕реЗ (рддрд░реЗрдо) рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдорд┐рд▓ рдХрд░ рдФрд░ рдмрд▓ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрдд рдХрд░ рджреБрдГрдЦрд░реВрдк рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░ рд╕реЗ рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрдВ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдп рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдп рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдорд╣реЛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ ! рддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд░реЛрджрд╕реНрдпреЛрдГ рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдордЪреНрдЫрд╛ рд╡реЛрдЪреЛ рдпреЗрди рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рдВ рд╕реБрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд┐рдВ рджрд┐рд╡реЛ рдиреДрдиреН рд╡реАрд╣рд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖реЛ рдЬрд╣рд┐ рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдВрд╜рд╣рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рд╡рдпрдВ рддрд░реЗрдо рд╡рд╛ рддрд░реЗрдо рддрд╡рд╛рд╡рд╕рд╛ рддрд░реЗрдо реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛) рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдорд╣рдГ) рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рд╕рдЦрд╛ рдорд╣рдГ рдкреВрдЬрдиреАрдпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрддреНрд╕рдореНрдмреБрджреНрдзреМ (рджреЗрд╡) рджрд╛рддрдГ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реЛ рджрд╛рддреДрдиреН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд┐рд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рд╡реЛрдЪрдГ) рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реЗрдГ (рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдореН) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдореН (рд░реЛрджрд╕реНрдпреЛрдГ) рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛрд░реНрдордзреНрдпреЗ (рд╡реАрд╣рд┐) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕реБрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд┐рдореН) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдВ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдВ рд╕реБрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдВ рд╡рд╛ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН (рдиреДрдиреН) рдирд╛рдпрдХрд╛рдиреН (рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ) рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреДрдиреН (рдЕрдВрд╣рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рдирд┐ (рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛) рджреБрдГрдЦрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдгрд┐ (рддрд░реЗрдо) рдЙрд▓реНрд▓рдЩреНрдШрдпреЗрдо (рддрд╛) рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рддрд░реЗрдо) (рддрд╡) (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпреЗрди (рддрд░реЗрдо) реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рдГ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддреНрдп рдмрд▓рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рддреНрдп рджреБрдГрдЦрд╕рд╛рдЧрд░рд╛рддреН рддрд░рдгреАрдпрдорд┐рддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреАрдиреЗ рдмрд▓ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░реВрди рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдВрдирд╛ рдЬрд┐рдВрдХреВрди рджреБрдГрдЦрд░реВрдкреА рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░ рдкрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛. рее резрез рее
